  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_d5191bdc-3b5c-4940-9d44-d9fdfb4989a9'
      });
    }

      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer6975612498845799203">Everyone, holder and dragonrider alike, pitched in to help--except Nerilka's father, who refused to share Fort Hold's bounty with the other holds. So, ashamed of her family and determined to do her part, Nerilka packed up medicines and supplies and sneaked off to aid her people.Her quest to help wherever she was most needed led her finally to Ruatha Hold, where Lord Alessa</span>
  <span id="freeText6975612498845799203" style="display:none">Everyone, holder and dragonrider alike, pitched in to help--except Nerilka's father, who refused to share Fort Hold's bounty with the other holds. So, ashamed of her family and determined to do her part, Nerilka packed up medicines and supplies and sneaked off to aid her people.Her quest to help wherever she was most needed led her finally to Ruatha Hold, where Lord Alessan was frantically inoculations against the dread plague.<br /><br />Nerilika had long ago abandoned the hope of mariage and a home of her own. Now she found happiness in being useful and appreciated---first the Healers and then Alessan made very clear that they were grateful for her help.<br /><br />She had no idea that her new path would change the course of her life forever.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2450631296" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5890622120321060699">Another fantastic story of Pern. This one is during the same time as Moreta. Nerilka is a beautiful soul who just can't stand how her father is with the people in her hold and the area around. Her father is a cold man that I haven't liked in either book. She has had enough of his nonsense, so she leaves the hold to find her own way. She is a brilliant character who puts meaning into her life by helping others. She is good at what she does and she thrives. Her mother taught her everything she kno</span>
  <span id="freeText5890622120321060699" style="display:none">Another fantastic story of Pern. This one is during the same time as Moreta. Nerilka is a beautiful soul who just can't stand how her father is with the people in her hold and the area around. Her father is a cold man that I haven't liked in either book. She has had enough of his nonsense, so she leaves the hold to find her own way. She is a brilliant character who puts meaning into her life by helping others. She is good at what she does and she thrives. Her mother taught her everything she knows and she is able to take that with her after the loss of her mother and sisters to the sickness that has decimated Pern. I thoroughly enjoyed this short story as a continuation of Moreta.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7258023-kaylabee?shelf=personal-library-catalog">personal-library-catalog</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2528212850" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13019908253421627145">I very much enjoyed this book! It was a nice break from McCaffrey’s third person voice- the story is told directly from Nerilka’s point of view. It also moved at a clipped pace, as its meant to be a companion book to Moreta. <br/><br/>It did feel like discovering the diary of someone who lived at a tumultuous time! I appreciated the added layers of understanding and story that this book provides to the Pern series. <br/><br/>Nerilka was a very calm and stalwart heroine- she knew her talents and was a grown woman wh</span>
  <span id="freeText13019908253421627145" style="display:none">I very much enjoyed this book! It was a nice break from McCaffrey’s third person voice- the story is told directly from Nerilka’s point of view. It also moved at a clipped pace, as its meant to be a companion book to Moreta. <br /><br />It did feel like discovering the diary of someone who lived at a tumultuous time! I appreciated the added layers of understanding and story that this book provides to the Pern series. <br /><br />Nerilka was a very calm and stalwart heroine- she knew her talents and was a grown woman who was willing to work hard. I felt like she was worthy of a book all her own- a strong woman who may not be considered “special” but IS special just by the good life she’s led. <br /><br />If I were five years younger I would’ve been disappointed in the romance of the book, but as a grown woman who has experienced the many different levels, trials, and heartbreaks of love I felt very satisfied with where Nerilka ended up and appreciated her relationship for its base of honor, hard work, and kindness and also approved of its stability and simplicity. I think most young girls have a very fairytale-Esque idea of love and marriage and thus get their hearts broken when that perfect vision is revealed to be a mirage. But Nerilkas love story felt real, and she was happy without any sort of death defying testaments to love or unbridled angst-filled passion. <br /><br />She led a simple life and I can appreciate that. <br /><br /><br />Anyways, all in all, I enjoyed the book and can’t wait to get into the next Pern book! </span>
  <a data-text-id="13019908253421627145" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer13623305862219184051">Ehh...I find as I return to Pern stories in my old age and re-read them that I like the depiction of the women's lot less and less. Nerilka has a strong voice, and this ancillary tale is engaging - but I genuinely disliked the depiction of her "romance", if you can even use that word, with Alessan.<br/><br/>More like 2.5 stars for the unfulfilling relationship Nerilka ends up in; but McCaffrey is still a talented writer with an impressive vocabulary, and I must award style points where points are due.</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Joan" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Joan" href="/user/show/3837733-joan">Joan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3160725581" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3954995447913287537">I was very annoyed with how much of the story was recycled from Moreta the first time I read it years ago, but not as annoyed this time. However, the fact remains much is recycled rather than original so I’m not going any higher than 3 stars. However, this is a rather decent story too. Nerilka has long since realized her lot in life is completely constrained by her parents’ decisions on her marriage and expects no happiness in life. Her one real friend was married to Alessan of Ruatha Hold until</span>
  <span id="freeText3954995447913287537" style="display:none">I was very annoyed with how much of the story was recycled from Moreta the first time I read it years ago, but not as annoyed this time. However, the fact remains much is recycled rather than original so I’m not going any higher than 3 stars. However, this is a rather decent story too. Nerilka has long since realized her lot in life is completely constrained by her parents’ decisions on her marriage and expects no happiness in life. Her one real friend was married to Alessan of Ruatha Hold until she died from being thrown off a horse. She is denied the chance to go to Ruatha when now widowed Lord Alessan holds his first gather even though 4 sisters went with their parents. <br />After Plague breaks out Nerilka is appalled all over again by the complete self centeredness of her father who breaks quarantine to return to Fort Hold and immediately gets his mistress and her family installed in her dead mother’s place. She is even more disgusted by his refusal to contribute necessary herbs to cure the flu epidemic. Stealing the herbal pharmaceuticals she and her dead sisters had prepared, she leaves Fort forever behind. What becomes of her will be shaped by her, not her disgusting father! <br />This theme of life going on after tragedy is in many ways a deeper theme than in Moreta. But Moreta is a more complex, layered story. I appreciate knowing what happened to Alessan as that was left unfinished in Moreta. The message that life can and must go on is always a good reminder, particularly since this could be read by adolescents who hopefully haven’t had to learn that hard lesson yet. Definitely recommended for Pern fans. </span>
  <a data-text-id="3954995447913287537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer11156221304494752889">I highly recommend reading <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61958.Moreta_Dragonlady_of_Pern__Pern___7_' title='Moreta Dragonlady of Pern (Pern, #7) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Moreta: Dragonlady of Pern</a> first, as it gives more of the overarching framework.<br/><br/>I have always liked the change to first-person POV, and telling the story from the vantage point of a very minor character fascinates me. <br/><br/>I normally like to start with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96463.The_Chronicles_of_Pern_First_Fall__Pern___12_' title='The Chronicles of Pern First Fall (Pern, #12) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Chronicles of Pern: First Fall</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/465904.Dragonsdawn__Pern___9_' title='Dragonsdawn (Pern, #9) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>Dragonsdawn</a>, working my way chronologically through Pern's history. But while in the middle of the COVID-19 pandemic, I decided to try reading this to determine if reading about plagues </span>
  <span id="freeText11156221304494752889" style="display:none">I highly recommend reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61958.Moreta_Dragonlady_of_Pern__Pern___7_" title="Moreta Dragonlady of Pern (Pern, #7) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Moreta: Dragonlady of Pern</a> first, as it gives more of the overarching framework.<br /><br />I have always liked the change to first-person POV, and telling the story from the vantage point of a very minor character fascinates me. <br /><br />I normally like to start with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/96463.The_Chronicles_of_Pern_First_Fall__Pern___12_" title="The Chronicles of Pern First Fall (Pern, #12) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">The Chronicles of Pern: First Fall</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/465904.Dragonsdawn__Pern___9_" title="Dragonsdawn (Pern, #9) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Dragonsdawn</a>, working my way chronologically through Pern's history. But while in the middle of the COVID-19 pandemic, I decided to try reading this to determine if reading about plagues is therapeutic as I heard. This was definitely good therapy for me. When the very first paragraph seemed to speak of me today, I knew I had to finish. And though the first half did include grief, it imparted several ways that people deal with the grief, which was enlightening. <br /><br />And the main reason I chose Nerilka's Story over Moreta's was because I knew this one ended much happier. And as a romance fan, I must have my happy ending. <br /><br />Favorite quotes:<br />"No one can challenge the fact that I have lived through a momentous time in Pern's history, a tragic time. I survived the Great Plague, though my heart still grieves for those lost to its virulence, and ever will." (p.1)<br /><br />"Sometimes one knows the drums are relaying good news, happy tidings. The beat seems brighter, higher-pitched, as if the very skins are singing with pleasure at their work. So if I fancied that the drums were weeping today, who could blame me?" (p.38)<br /><br />"I suspect it would put a blight on our relationship when he did. But that was really his problem. Mine was getting into my own bed, [sic] and not wishing that there was someone who might care to tuck me in." (p.134)</span>

<div id="review_3257405845" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3257405845" />
    <a title="prcardi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43250213-prcardi"><img alt="prcardi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1471708128p2/43250213.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3257405845?book_show_action=true">Apr 01, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="prcardi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="prcardi" href="/user/show/43250213-prcardi">prcardi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=pg-13">pg-13</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=other-world">other-world</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43250213-prcardi?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3257405845" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8040461012456914531">Storyline: 1/5<br/>Characters: 3/5<br/>Writing Style: 3/5<br/>World: 2/5<br/><br/>The possibilities promised by the parallel tale format are enticing. See the other point of view, find out about another’s struggles, learn about entirely new relationships and connections, see what happened to minor compatriots or major ones off-page. <i>Nerilka’s Story</i>, a parallel tale to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3162371949' rel='nofollow noopener'><i>Moreta: Dragonlady of Pern</i> </a>, supplies only a few of these and those only perfunctorily. This is not a story that can be read as a stand-alone. In lieu of </span>
  <span id="freeText8040461012456914531" style="display:none">Storyline: 1/5<br />Characters: 3/5<br />Writing Style: 3/5<br />World: 2/5<br /><br />The possibilities promised by the parallel tale format are enticing. See the other point of view, find out about another’s struggles, learn about entirely new relationships and connections, see what happened to minor compatriots or major ones off-page. <i>Nerilka’s Story</i>, a parallel tale to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3162371949" rel="nofollow noopener"><i>Moreta: Dragonlady of Pern</i> </a>, supplies only a few of these and those only perfunctorily. This is not a story that can be read as a stand-alone. In lieu of development and buildup, McCaffrey gives a long, dry prologue that introduces the world of Pern as presented in the previous books, dutifully cataloging its professions and culture. This prologue does not, however, review the events of <i>Moreta</i>. This was an odd decision on the part of the author since <i>Nerilka’s Story</i> is written as if the reader does indeed know of those events, McCaffrey taking little time to build up suspense or fully explain happenings. The parallel tale itself has little new of interest. There’s no great discovery or revelation. There’s no delightful intersection. There’s no surprising twist. Instead, what is presented are the bits that seemed to have been left out of <i>Moreta</i>. If you were a teenage girl desiring to read a female author, already enthralled with the lands of Pern, having loved <i>Moretta</i> and wanting to know every detail – especially details about another strong, female character – then this book was probably eagerly received and devoured. McCaffrey’s talents are showcased with the circumstances around the main character. Though the characters themselves were nothing exceptional, the situations and interactions they are put through generate some particularly emotional scenes. Otherwise, this mostly read as a very uninspired and lazy attempt by the author to add another <i>Pern</i> book to the series while committing only minimal effort. This was not worth being considered a new Pern book, and it showed the author more as the marketer of a product than an author penning new, fantastical tales.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8040461012456914531" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_324912256" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/324912256" />
    <a title="Sara" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/400197-sara"><img alt="Sara" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1264634306p2/400197.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/324912256?book_show_action=true">May 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sara" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sara" href="/user/show/400197-sara">Sara</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/400197-sara?shelf=fiction">fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/400197-sara?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer324912256" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3635524999001544962">This novella, set in McCaffrey’s epic world of Pern, is stylistically more like a Regency romance than a science-fiction short story. McCaffrey provides an prologue which explains the setting and historical background of the story, but it is more confusing than explanatory, and readers would do well to skip to the story itself.<br/><br/>Nerilka is one of the many daughters of the Lord of Fort Hold, and as a plain, hard-working girl, harbors no romantic thoughts of a lavish marriage and escape from Fort Ho</span>
  <span id="freeText3635524999001544962" style="display:none">This novella, set in McCaffrey’s epic world of Pern, is stylistically more like a Regency romance than a science-fiction short story. McCaffrey provides an prologue which explains the setting and historical background of the story, but it is more confusing than explanatory, and readers would do well to skip to the story itself.<br /><br />Nerilka is one of the many daughters of the Lord of Fort Hold, and as a plain, hard-working girl, harbors no romantic thoughts of a lavish marriage and escape from Fort Hold. She spends most of her time gathering and preparing medicinal plants for the healers. Her parents and four sisters are visiting another Hold when a disease and quarantine strikes Pern. Nerilka’s father, in defiance of the quarantine, leaves his dying wife and daughters to return home to Fort Hold, where upon hearing of their death, installs his mistress, Anella, and her extended family in the Fort. Nerilka, appalled at his actions and his refusal to send supplies from their overflowing stockroom to those in need, disguises herself and takes medical supplies to those in need, eventually coming to Ruatha Hold, where she becomes a valued member of the Healers.<br /><br />Published in the mid 1980′s, the black and white illustrations are rather laughable. I remembered this book as being a charming little story, but upon re-reading, found that it has not aged well — which is funny, seeing that it is science fiction set in the distant future. Perhaps it is best read after consuming several of McCaffrey’s Pern novels and getting in to the proper mindset.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3635524999001544962" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Chris Gager" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5295008-chris-gager"><img alt="Chris Gager" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1307204529p2/5295008.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1635098720?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris Gager" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris Gager" href="/user/show/5295008-chris-gager">Chris Gager</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780345331595" href="/book/show/2090085.Nerilka_s_Story">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1635098720" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6788022497755749890">Started this last night after finishing "Paris Review #183." Rescued from somewhere - maybe the town transfer station book shelves. Safe to say that Anne M.'s work never appeared in THAT periodical! This is my third Pern read. So far I've enjoyed the late Ms. McCaffrey's prose - easy to read and enjoyable. I like that she leans heavily on female protagonists too. "Dragondrums" featured a Ray Liotta look-alike in the cover art and this one features a Nerilka who looks like Sandra Bernhard with a </span>
  <span id="freeText6788022497755749890" style="display:none">Started this last night after finishing "Paris Review #183." Rescued from somewhere - maybe the town transfer station book shelves. Safe to say that Anne M.'s work never appeared in THAT periodical! This is my third Pern read. So far I've enjoyed the late Ms. McCaffrey's prose - easy to read and enjoyable. I like that she leans heavily on female protagonists too. "Dragondrums" featured a Ray Liotta look-alike in the cover art and this one features a Nerilka who looks like Sandra Bernhard with a nose job - very tall.<br /><br />Finished last night with this rather brief and sketchy Pern tale. It was ok ... nothing special but entertaining enough to get a 3* rating(2.75 actually). The story is very similar to Lessa's in "Weyr Search"(the first part of Dragonflight): underappreciated/hidden young woman finds her destiny(and a husband) etc. As others have noted there's not a lot of dragon action in this one. Not a lot of action at all as a matter for fact. As I said, this is not any kind of a Pern epic. Like "Dragondrums," it's a side story. Moreta is a major Pern character in another book, while Nerilka appears briefly. Here it's the opposite.<br /><br />- The narrative can be a bit confusing at times, especially when some very bad things happen near the end. Important details seem to be skimmed over. Dag's leg is splinted but we aren't told why. I assume the explanation is in the "Moreta ..." book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="6788022497755749890" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2799775723" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2799775723" />
    <a title="Bonnie Jean" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4865823-bonnie-jean"><img alt="Bonnie Jean" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1487426039p2/4865823.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2799775723?book_show_action=true">May 03, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bonnie Jean" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bonnie Jean" href="/user/show/4865823-bonnie-jean">Bonnie Jean</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4865823-bonnie-jean?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4865823-bonnie-jean?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4865823-bonnie-jean?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4865823-bonnie-jean?shelf=girl-power">girl-power</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4865823-bonnie-jean?shelf=angst">angst</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2799775723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14717691550071175209">Super quick read- took me only a couple hours to finish- but surprisingly one of the better Pern novels. I'm a bit sad I missed this one on my first read through- I'm pretty sure teenage me would have enjoyed Nerilka's story even more than adult me did. This is exactly the sort of novella that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127586.The_White_Dragon__Pern___3_' title='The White Dragon (Pern, #3) by Anne McCaffrey' rel='nofollow noopener'>The White Dragon</a> left me wishing for. I would have loved to see a novella like this from Mirrim's POV also before the series had ended- a background story, not 100% necessary to moving the plot forward, bu</span>
  <span id="freeText14717691550071175209" style="display:none">Super quick read- took me only a couple hours to finish- but surprisingly one of the better Pern novels. I'm a bit sad I missed this one on my first read through- I'm pretty sure teenage me would have enjoyed Nerilka's story even more than adult me did. This is exactly the sort of novella that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/127586.The_White_Dragon__Pern___3_" title="The White Dragon (Pern, #3) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">The White Dragon</a> left me wishing for. I would have loved to see a novella like this from Mirrim's POV also before the series had ended- a background story, not 100% necessary to moving the plot forward, but helping to flesh out a character who deserves to have her story told from a sympathetic perspective.<br /><br />Nerilka's story is not exactly a standalone novel- I am not sure all of the events of the novel would have made complete sense if I hadn't just read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/61958.Moreta_Dragonlady_of_Pern__Pern___7_" title="Moreta Dragonlady of Pern (Pern, #7) by Anne McCaffrey" rel="nofollow noopener">Moreta: Dragonlady of Pern</a> first- but I actually like this behind the scenes novella much better than I did the actual full length story about Moreta. Well, mostly better. The romance between Nerilka and Alessan is... odd. Their relationship has a very troubling start to it, even if it eventually finds its way to a healthier place. This is not the first Pern novel that has left me feeling like their society could benefit from a specialized Psychological Healers Hall (but evidently all knowledge of psychology has been lost over the centuries? *sigh*) . Aside from that, though, I overall found Nerilka's character more sympathetic than many of the characters in Moreta's book, so the fact that I liked this novella so much may, in part, just be that it really benefitted from the style of being written in Nerilka's 1st person POV. Anne McCaffrey evidently just writes angsty young women well. ;)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14717691550071175209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15830791445999975599">Lady Nerilka is a daughter of the Lord of Hold Fort. She is not an attractive girl. Her mother has trained her to be a healer for the Hold: collecting herbs, making medicines, and keeping a still room. Lord and Lady and several of Nerilka's sister attend a gather at Rutha Hold, where a deadly virus is running rampant through Pern. Nerilka's father returns home without his wife and children, who die at Rutha.<br/>Nerilka uses her skills to try to help the Healer's Hall. Her father declares no one is a</span>
  <span id="freeText15830791445999975599" style="display:none">Lady Nerilka is a daughter of the Lord of Hold Fort. She is not an attractive girl. Her mother has trained her to be a healer for the Hold: collecting herbs, making medicines, and keeping a still room. Lord and Lady and several of Nerilka's sister attend a gather at Rutha Hold, where a deadly virus is running rampant through Pern. Nerilka's father returns home without his wife and children, who die at Rutha.<br />Nerilka uses her skills to try to help the Healer's Hall. Her father declares no one is allowed to enter the Hold from outside. There are people camped at the gates who are sick and need medicines. Once a person leaves the Hold, they may not return. Nerilka disguises herself as a drudge and takes medicines to the encampment where she works tirelessly to help the sick.<br />A syrum was developed to immunize against the virus. Nerilka receives the vaccine before she leaves the Hold.<br />In a roundabout way, Nerilka arrives at Rutha Hold and immediately begins to help. She goes by the name of Rill.<br />Please read the book to find out what happens to her.</span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2119194841" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18197324585523794856">I love the Pern series of books. This particular tale in the series is very enjoyable, and a quick read. The reason I enjoy this book so much is due to it's intertwined connection the Moreta story. In the first two trilogies of this series the Legend of Moreta's ride is often mentioned. Then, Anne McCaffrey actually writes the story behind that legend. Now, the brief novella of Nerilka takes and almost non-existent character from the Moreta story and retells the tale from her point of view. Betw</span>
  <span id="freeText18197324585523794856" style="display:none">I love the Pern series of books. This particular tale in the series is very enjoyable, and a quick read. The reason I enjoy this book so much is due to it's intertwined connection the Moreta story. In the first two trilogies of this series the Legend of Moreta's ride is often mentioned. Then, Anne McCaffrey actually writes the story behind that legend. Now, the brief novella of Nerilka takes and almost non-existent character from the Moreta story and retells the tale from her point of view. Between the second perspective on these historic events in Pern's history and the engaging story telling style of McCaffrey, this is a must read for the true Pern lover.</span>

<div id="review_2210145402" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2210145402" />
    <a title="Alison Swearingen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20693853-alison-swearingen"><img alt="Alison Swearingen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583978701p2/20693853.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2210145402?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer912212126285995148"><strong>Short and sweet second telling</strong><br/><br/>Paired with Moreta's story, this quick read gives a second point of view of the terrible toll on Pern and it's people when plague hits during the years of a fall. <br/><br/>To be honest, I'm not sure why the author decided to make this a separate book as it could have been Incorporated into Moreta's story without having to rewrite parts of the storyline. <br/><br/>That said, this quick read tied up some lingering questions and that was worth that bit of duplicated reading.</span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2158484290" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17940099813676823974">If McCaffrey and taken Moreta and Nerilka and somehow made them into one book with alternating perspectives, I think it would have made a much more engaging story. It gets a little tedious reading the same dialogue in this book that was in Moreta. And again, the ending of this book is spoiled in the previous one, so there are no surprises. It's a nice enough story, but not one of the best in the Pern series.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer6443878962016647189">This is a short parallel novella to <i>Moreta Dragonlady of Pern</i>. <br/><br/>It was an interesting read but not a necessary read in the grand scape of the Pern series.<br/><br/>Nerilka is the daughter of the Lord Holder of Fort Hold. She is left behind there when the plague breaks out and is spared illness but had to deal with her mother's death, her father quickly taking his mistress as his new wife, and her father's insolence about the plague and sharing supplies. </span>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2854961741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14777135066977624114"><strong>Love this book</strong><br/><br/>Not an adventurous tale or a steamy romance, just a quiet story about an ordinary person caught up in the aftermath of a disaster she doesn’t really understand. No extraordinary powers here, even the dragons are kind of peripheral to the story. There’s just people, doing their best. As a side note, you really should read Moreta first to understand the events going on around Nerilka.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('g3TCqLUDJgxou+CaBPIYJG5HQ1t1a8pZ8/DTCPF/4bn/PYfbRTxjsYZS83Ojijmci3pz/l5UV3gQRQt0tIPylQ==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('S08tGdVQhX+Kdbxl3fTxtaJfbouZAY9SBR3hrD3OKxI3BmhqJW/AwmScr4x6jNANR2JeLrI+EnPmqDnQeDI4Pg==')})

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey">About Anne McCaffrey</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1599324585p3/26.jpg);'></div>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/26.Anne_McCaffrey">Anne McCaffrey
</a></div>

followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17248117236018820393">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br/><br/>Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br/><br/>Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High Scho</span>
  <span id="freeText17248117236018820393" style="display:none">Anne McCaffrey was born on April 1st, 1926, in Cambridge, Massachusetts.<br /><br />Her parents were George Herbert McCaffrey, BA, MA PhD (Harvard), Colonel USA Army (retired), and Anne Dorothy McElroy McCaffrey, estate agent. She had two brothers: Hugh McCaffrey (deceased 1988), Major US Army, and Kevin Richard McCaffrey, still living.<br /><br />Anne was educated at Stuart Hall in Staunton Virginia, Montclair High School in Montclair, New Jersey, and graduated cum laude from Radcliffe College, majoring in Slavonic Languages and Literatures.<br /><br />Her working career included Liberty Music Shops and Helena Rubinstein (1947-1952). She married in 1950 and had three children: Alec Anthony, b. 1952, Todd, b.1956, and Georgeanne, b.1959.<br /><br />Anne McCaffrey’s first story was published by Sam Moskowitz in Science Fiction + Magazine and her first novel was published by Ballantine Books in 1967. By the time the three children of her marriage were comfortably in school most of the day, she had already achieved enough success with short stories to devote full time to writing. Her first novel, Restoree, was written as a protest against the absurd and unrealistic portrayals of women in s-f novels in the 50s and early 60s. It is, however, in the handling of broader themes and the worlds of her imagination, particularly the two series The Ship Who Sang and the fourteen novels about the Dragonriders of Pern that Ms. McCaffrey’s talents as a story-teller are best displayed.<br /><br />She died at the age of 85, after suffering a massive stroke on 21 November 2011.<br /><br />Obituaries: <a href="http://www.locusmag.com/News/2011/11/anne-mccaffrey-1926-2011/" rel="nofollow noopener">Locus</a>, <a href="http://www.mediabistro.com/galleycat/anne-mccaffrey-has-died_b42826" rel="nofollow noopener">GalleyCat</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17248117236018820393" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
